City Government's Reply to Japan Still Under Serious Consideration, Not Yet Sent Out Last Night 131

Regarding the matter of the City Government's reply to the Japanese Consul's protest, the Japanese side has repeatedly urged the City Government. However, the City Government considers the four demands of the Japanese Consul to be of great importance and is currently seeking opinions from all sectors and giving them serious consideration. As of last night, the reply had not yet been sent out. It is rumored that the City Government has a firm grasp on maintaining peace and it is hoped that the situation will not escalate. The reply to Japan is expected to be sent out in a day or two. Secretary-General Yu of the City Government visited the Japanese Consul-General yesterday to discuss a quick resolution to the Sino-Japanese negotiations. Shirai stated that there was no 48-hour deadline for a reply. Regarding the letter of protest submitted by the Japanese Consulate to the City Government regarding the assault on Japanese monks on the 18th, the City Government has not yet delivered its reply to the Japanese Consulate as of yesterday because it still needs to carefully consider the four demands. Furthermore, Mayor Wu specifically dispatched Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, accompanied by Mr. Yin Rugeng, to visit Japanese Consul-General Murai Kuramatsu at the Japanese Consulate at approximately 3 PM yesterday. Mr. Murai and Vice-Consul Iguchi met with them in the Consul-General's office. The meeting lasted approximately two hours, and they departed after 5 PM. According to Japanese Vice-Consul Iguchi and Mr. Shirai Yasushi, Secretary-General Yu and Yin Rugeng's visit to Consul-General Murai Kuramatsu was to discuss how to quickly resolve the Sino-Japanese negotiations. They added that the Japanese side had not stated that there was a 48-hour deadline for a reply to the protest. (New Sound News Agency)

Japanese Warships and Aircraft Continue to Arrive; Warships Rush to the Yangtze River

The number of Japanese warships stationed in Shanghai has reached eleven. Now, the cruiser Yubari is being dispatched, leading three destroyer squadrons, totaling thirteen ships, from the 22nd, 21st, and 30th squadrons to Shanghai. They have already departed from Sasebo, but had not yet arrived by night. According to Japanese sources, these three Japanese squadrons may arrive in Shanghai today. The naval commander of the First Overseas Dispatch Unit stationed in Shanghai, considering the deteriorating situation, dispatched one warship to the lower reaches of the Yangtze River the day before yesterday. Yesterday afternoon at 3:40 PM, he also ordered the cruiser Hirado to load military equipment and marines in Shanghai and rush to Nanjing to be stationed there.

Military Aircraft Arrive in Shanghai

The Japanese aviation unit had previously brought one squadron on the Notoro Maru. Now, six more naval aircraft are being transferred from Sasebo to Shanghai. It was pre-arranged with the Japan Mail Steamship Company to transport them in two batches. The first aircraft arrived at this port on the Shanghai Maru at 3 PM yesterday afternoon. It was unloaded at the Wayson Wharf and immediately transported to Hongkou. The pilots had already arrived in Shanghai beforehand. It was decided yesterday that the second batch of three aircraft would arrive at the end of this month on the Nagasaki Maru. All six aircraft are military fighter planes.

Shigemitsu to Arrive in Shanghai at the End of the Month

Japanese Ambassador to China, Shigemitsu Aoi, previously returned to Japan to report on the state of negotiations with China and to meet with the new Foreign Minister Yoshizawa. Now, due to the extremely tense situation in Shanghai, Shigemitsu has sent a telegram to Shanghai stating that he will take the Japan Mail Steamship Nagasaki Maru and is expected to arrive in Shanghai at the end of the month.

Japanese Nationals Evacuate from Various Locations

Japanese consuls in various locations have recently issued advisories ordering Japanese nationals in Wuhu, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, and Hangzhou to evacuate from those ports within one or two days and gather in Shanghai, from where they will return to their home country. Six or seventy Japanese nationals from Suzhou have already left Suzhou for Shanghai yesterday. Japanese nationals from Wuhu, Nanjing, Hangzhou, and Zhenjiang are expected to arrive in Shanghai in the next two days.

Navigation at Wusong Remains Normal

Rumors arose in Shanghai yesterday, stating that from 6 PM, ships would not be allowed to sail from Wusong, and Shanghai-bound ships would have to sail earlier or cease night navigation. After investigation, it has been learned that while defenses at Wusong have indeed been strengthened, there are no restrictions on ship traffic. Therefore, ships such as the Ningbo liner sailed as scheduled yesterday without impediment.

Foreign Warships Increase Their Presence in Shanghai

Since the outbreak of the serious situation in Shanghai, various countries, considering the interests at stake, cannot afford to ignore it. The United States Asiatic Fleet first dispatched the cruiser Houston, leading the destroyers Peary and Macdonough, from Little Luzon. They are expected to arrive in Shanghai today. One of the ships, upon arriving at Wusong, will proceed to Nanjing. The United Kingdom has also dispatched a destroyer from Hong Kong, which arrived in Shanghai at noon.

Japanese Marines Landed in Pudong Yesterday, It Is Said

To protect the Japanese-Chinese cotton mill. After negotiations, they withdrew after two hours. The situation in Shanghai has become increasingly serious recently. Yesterday morning at around 11 AM, over twenty Japanese marines landed at Lujiazui in Pudong, claiming to be there to protect the First and Second Factories of the Japanese-Chinese cotton mill in the area. They did not withdraw until after 1 PM, after negotiations by our side. The situation is described below:

Chinese Police Protect the Japanese-Chinese Cotton Mill in Lujiazui, Pudong

In addition to Chinese workers, there are many Japanese staff in the First and Second Factories of the Japanese-Chinese cotton mill. Since the burning of the Sanyou Industrial Company factory, tensions have risen sharply in Shanghai. The Japanese staff of the cotton mill immediately stated that the factory was not without danger and required strong protection. The Third District Public Security Bureau, which has jurisdiction over the area, has provided very tight protection for the factory.

Japanese Troops Landed

At 11:30 AM yesterday, Japanese marines suddenly arrived by ship and landed at Lujiazui. There were over twenty marines, each carrying machine guns and rifles. After landing, they went to the front of the Japanese-Chinese cotton mill and patrolled back and forth. The nearby residents were greatly alarmed.

Negotiations Between Authorities and Japanese Marines Regarding the Landing

Zhang Mingqin, the district head of the Third District, immediately led police officers to the site to negotiate with the marines. The marines stated that the Japanese staff inside the Japanese-Chinese cotton mill were in danger, fearing that Chinese people would harm them, so they came to protect them. District Head Zhang replied that the factory was located within the Chinese territory and that the Chinese authorities had the strength to maintain local security and protect foreign nationals, so there was no need for Japanese troops to assist. The marines then withdrew.

Japanese Marines Withdrew After Negotiations with District Head Zhang

The attitude of the Japanese marines was initially quite strong, but they suddenly withdrew on their own, completely leaving the shore and boarding their ship at around 1:30 PM.

Reported to the City Government

After the incident, District Head Zhang immediately reported the situation to the Public Security Bureau. At this time, Japanese Vice-Consul Shirai Yasushi also visited Director Wen Yingxing and Section Chief Shen, briefly discussing the matter and hoping that the Sino-Japanese conflict would be resolved as soon as possible. Director Wen then went to the City Government at 3 PM to report on the incident.

Yesterday the Preparations in Shanghai Were Stepped Up; Defenses Were Tightly Arranged in Zhabei

Since the 24th of this month, barricades of sandbags and barbed wire have been erected at key intersections in Zhabei. However, the sandbags were piled too low, so on the day before yesterday, the Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatched police officers to lead laborers, using a large number of sacks, to fill them with sand and mud in the open space north of the Huzhou Guild Hall, and transport them to various locations to pile up, and to raise the height of the existing barricades at intersections. Those that have been completed, such as the intersections of Zhongxing Road and Gonghe Xin Road, Yongxing Small Road, Yongxing Branch Road, and Yuyingtang Road, are all sandbags. From the Huzhou Guild Hall eastward, there are barbed wire fences. To the south, from the intersections of Yongxing Road, Xiangshan Road, and Huiwen Road and Zhongxing Road, in addition to extremely high sandbags, there are also barbed wire fences. During the day, the middle section of the barbed wire fence is removed to allow pedestrian and vehicle traffic. After 12:00 midnight, or when necessary, it is used to block traffic. Multiple barbed wire fences have also been erected at the intersections of Gongxing Road and Baotong Road. Regarding Baoshan Road, in addition to the extremely tight sandbag and barbed wire barricades erected north of the Baoshan Road Railway Station, there are also similar defenses at the Yokohama Bridge, also known as the Baoshan Bridge (at the northern end of Baoshan Road). Some defenses have also been erected about ten yards south of the Nanguang Alley intersection (in front of the Small Vegetable Market), which is a little over ten yards away from the Baoshan Bridge. Other defenses are either already in place or are being constructed. The arrangements are extremely tight. However, trains on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Nanjing lines continue to run as usual, arriving at their stations on time.

Emergency Meeting of the Zhabei Security Corps

In view of the serious situation of the Shanghai Incident and the importance of defense, the Zhabei Security Corps held an emergency meeting yesterday afternoon at 3 PM at its headquarters on Nanxing Road. Those present included Corps Commander Wang Binyan, Deputy Commander Gu Zhuxuan, First Squadron Leader Jin Xipin (stationed at the headquarters), Second Squadron Leader Xu Youtang (Shuncheng Road), Third Squadron Leader Mo Meiqing (Baoshan Road), Fourth Squadron Leader Xing Minyi (Xingjia Bridge), Fifth Squadron Leader Zhu Renzhai (Hujia Muqiao), Sixth Squadron Leader Cheng Jingchuan (Qingyun Road), Seventh Squadron Leader Chen Yuxin (Panjiawan), and Eighth Squadron Leader Gu Xiqi (Hanzhong Road). They exchanged views on the defense of northern Shanghai and discussed the matter in great detail. The meeting adjourned at 7 PM.

Defense Meeting of the Nanshi Security Corps

In light of the urgent situation in recent days, the Shanghai Security Corps held a defense meeting yesterday afternoon at 3 PM at the headquarters of the Hunan District Security Corps. Wang Binyan, Yao Mulian, and others attended. As a result, several decisions were made regarding the direction of defense, instructing the various district corps to follow them. If necessary, they will cooperate with the military and police authorities to maintain local security under their control.

Safety Issues in the Concessions: The Municipal Council Has Made Adequate Preparations

Mr. Feetham stated that yesterday, due to the rampant rumors, a Pacific News Agency reporter specifically visited Mr. Feetham, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Council. He was received and questioned about the re-publication of the Republican Daily and the attitude towards the anti-Japanese movement. Mr. Feetham replied that the Municipal Council's purpose is solely to maintain law and order. Previously, because the Republican Daily published news about the Japanese marines, it caused disputes. The Municipal Council did not want to cause even more serious misunderstandings because of this, so it advised the newspaper to suspend publication in good faith. If the Sino-Japanese

Page 14

incident can be resolved satisfactorily, then there will be no problem with resuming publication. If the Sino-Japanese relationship unfortunately deteriorates, even to the point of conflict, then that is something that we cannot decide at the moment. The reporter also asked, "There are widespread rumors abroad, roughly saying that the Japanese side is demanding the cessation of the anti-Japanese movement; otherwise, they may prepare for direct action. What is the attitude of the Municipal Council?" He replied, "This may be purely external rumors. The Japanese side and Commander Shiozawa himself have not made a demand to the Municipal Council to disband the anti-Japanese associations, and I have not made such a suggestion either. The Municipal Council will definitely not suppress the patriotic movement of the Chinese people. The rumors mentioned above may refer to rumors of direct action by the Japanese side towards the Chinese territory. In short, regarding responsibility within the Concession, the Municipal Council will do its utmost to prevent Sino-Japanese conflict or actions that disrupt law and order." He was asked, "It is rumored that you, in your personal capacity, will act as a mediator in this Sino-Japanese incident. Is this true?" He replied, "I would be very happy to do so in my personal capacity, but it seems that there will not be more serious facts discovered at the moment. If there are any within the Concession, the Municipal Council will do its best to ensure the safety of the residents of the Concession and is even willing to do everything possible to seek an early resolution to the Sino-Japanese incident."

The Municipal Council is on Alert

The Shanghai Times reported that after discussions last night (26th) with the commanders of the British and American forces stationed in Shanghai and the commander of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps, the Municipal Council authorities decided to make practical preparations to protect life and property within the International Settlement. The first step is to build barbed wire fences at key points around the perimeter of the Concession. This plan is only for precautionary purposes. If the situation becomes tense, it will be expanded. It was also agreed that if an emergency occurs, the British army will take over the defense of the Western District, the US Marines will be responsible for patrolling the Suzhou Creek area, and the Volunteer Corps will protect the Central District. Similar protection plans will also be implemented in the Northern and Eastern Districts.

US Marines on Alert

The Greater Shanghai Evening News reported that Japanese Fleet Commander Rear Admiral Shiozawa met with officials from the Municipal Council and the commander of the Shanghai Defense Forces this morning (27th). The results were not released. It is reported that the Fourth Marine Regiment stationed in Shanghai has been ordered to be on alert. 50% of their passes have been revoked. The remaining 50% are allowed to leave the camp, but may not go beyond the Garden Bridge or Edinburgh Road.

Kong Xiangxi and Li Zongren Arrive in Shanghai Last Night, Sun Ke Still Makes No Statements, Chen Mingshu Scheduled to Arrive in Shanghai This Morning

After the resignation of President of the Executive Yuan Sun Ke, the Central Government repeatedly sent senior officials to Shanghai to persuade him to stay. Kong Xiangxi, bearing the mandate of Chiang Kai-shek, arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing at 8 AM yesterday, carrying a second personal letter from Chiang to Sun, urging Sun to go to Nanjing as soon as possible to discuss national affairs together. Sun has made no statement regarding reinstatement. Vice President of the Executive Yuan Chen Mingshu was also ordered by the Central Government to come to Shanghai and is scheduled to arrive this morning to meet with Sun and make a final attempt to persuade him.

Lin Kanghou Discusses the Central Government Loan Issue, Shanghai Can Raise Up to 8 Million Yuan, the Issue Can Be Resolved if Someone Is in Charge at the Central Level

According to Finance News Agency reporters who interviewed Finance Official Lin Kanghou yesterday, the Shanghai financial community plans to raise 8 million yuan for the Central Government loan. The allocation method is as follows: the Central Bank, Bank of Communications, and Bank of China will provide a total of 4 million yuan, various commercial banks will provide 2 million yuan, the money industry will provide 1 million yuan, and the Stock Exchange Federation will provide 1 million yuan. The Central Bank, Bank of Communications, and Bank of China are generally expected to have no major problems. The Stock Exchange Federation has requested to reduce its share to 500,000 yuan, and the money industry has requested that it be reduced to 500,000 yuan as well. Some commercial banks have also requested to reduce their numbers. In general, the amount of 8 million yuan may be able to be raised. However, after the resignations of Executive Yuan President Sun and Finance Minister Huang, no one is in charge at the Central level, causing the loan issue, which had been successfully negotiated, to come to a halt midway. The loan issue needs to be resolved after someone is in charge at the Central level. After Minister of Military Affairs He Yingqin discussed loan-related matters at the Ministry of Finance's Shanghai office the night before last, he has already returned to Nanjing. Today, the Bankers' Association will hold a meeting, and I (Lin, referring to himself) will attend to report on the discussions with Minister He.

Yang Shuzhuang to Return to Shanghai Immediately from Hong Kong

According to Jiji News, after resigning from the position of Minister of the Navy, National Government Committee Member Yang Shuzhuang has repeatedly and firmly declined the position of Chairman of the Fujian Provincial Government. He has been suffering from a severe lung illness and frequently coughs up blood, so he specifically moved to Hong Kong to recuperate. Now, because there are private matters to be dealt with in Shanghai, he is rushing to Shanghai and is scheduled to arrive on February 12. We have already received a personal telegram from Mr. Yang stating this.

There Will Be British Troops Coming to Shanghai, But It Has Nothing to Do with the Situation

The Shanghai Times reported that the First Battalion of the British Wiltshire Regiment will arrive in Shanghai on Saturday and Sunday on the Lancashire transport ship from Egypt, replacing the Royal Scottish Regiment. It has nothing to do with the situation in China. The current situation in Shanghai does not justify increasing the number of British troops. In addition to the 270 men who have joined the First Battalion arriving from Egypt, the Royal Scottish Regiment will return to England on February 6 on the Lancashire transport ship. When the ship arrives in Shanghai on Saturday and Sunday, it will also carry 150 troops replacing the Tianjin garrison. After arriving in Shanghai, they will temporarily reside in the Hongkou barracks. Therefore, all the arrangements made in the Hongkou barracks these days have nothing to do with the current situation.

Japanese Cotton Mills to Close Down Completely Today

Regarding the reports about the Japanese-run cotton mills in this port preparing to suspend operations, this newspaper has reported on them repeatedly. Yesterday, the China Cotton Spinning Association held an emergency meeting and decided to completely close down the mills today (28th). It is reported that all 24 Japanese nationals at the Wusong Huafeng Cotton Mill also left the factory yesterday to return to their home country. Over a thousand workers were paid their wages yesterday afternoon.

The Wusong Huafeng Cotton Mill Suspends Operations Due to Martial Law from Today; Authorities Dispatch Personnel to Mediate

The Wusong Yunzaobang Japanese-owned Huafeng Cotton Mill (i.e., the Eighth Factory of the Japanese-Chinese Cotton Spinning Co., Ltd.) has 25,600 cotton spindles and 11,520 yarn spindles, and employs over 2,000 Chinese workers. Since the start of the National Salvation Movement and the boycott, the stock has piled up. Now, due to the current situation and the imposition of martial law in Wusong, which is inconvenient for work, a formal notice was issued yesterday officially announcing the suspension of operations from today. Personnel have been dispatched to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to request protection. Upon hearing the news, all the workers, fearing that they would be unable to make a living if operations were suspended once the end of the year arrives, have reported to the Eighth District Party Headquarters and the Eighth District Cotton Spinning Industry Union, requesting assistance. The Municipal Public Security Bureau and Social Affairs Bureau have scheduled to dispatch personnel today to jointly visit and find ways to mediate.

The Navy's New Aircraft, Jiangfeng, Conducts Test Flight

The Navy Aircraft Manufacturing Department completed the Jianghe and Jiangfeng, two new aircraft, last month. The Jianghe has already undergone a test flight and is now being modified with land wheels. The Jiangfeng also underwent a test flight yesterday afternoon at 3 PM at the Longhua Pumi Water Aerodrome. Director of the Naval Aviation Department Shen Dexie personally piloted the aircraft, circling the sky once before landing on the water surface. The results were quite good.

Deputy Captain of the Yuzhang Has Been Ordered to Report to Nanjing; If the Sunken Ship Is Difficult to Salvage, It Is Proposed to Be Blown Up

Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan came to Shanghai yesterday and stated that most of the naval vessels are currently being repaired in Shanghai and there have been no major movements. The Yuzhang torpedo boat, which sank on Qingti Reef in Tongzhou, is currently being salvaged. However, the sunken area is dozens of feet deep and cannot be seen at all. Furthermore, a telegram was received today stating that the seabed sediment in that area is rapidly shifting, which will increase the difficulty if the ship is submerged by sand. Therefore, these matters are currently being considered. If the ship cannot be salvaged, it is proposed to remove the detachable parts and then destroy the ship's hull. Otherwise, the main thoroughfare will obstruct ships. However, the loss from destroying the Yuzhang would naturally be greater than salvaging it. Feng Zhou, the deputy captain of the ship, has been ordered to report to Nanjing and is currently being interrogated by a special court organized by the Navy Department. If the point of Commander Feng's negligence is clarified after the interrogation, there will be punishment, but this is not yet known.

The National Goods Promotion Association Held a Regular Meeting Yesterday

The 15th meeting of the National Goods Promotion Grand Alliance Committee was held yesterday afternoon at 3 PM at the Nine Mu Di Association Hall. Fourteen people, including Shu Huizhen, attended. Zhu Zhenhan was elected as chairman. After performing the formalities, the following cases were resolved: (1) Assisting in the Sanyou Industrial Company arson case: It was resolved to send a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Industry, as well as the Songhu Garrison Command, the City Government, and the Social Affairs Bureau, to effectively protect national goods factories, lodge a serious protest with Japan, and report the facts of the riot to the League of Nations. (2) Reviewing the organizational outline: It was resolved to pass it. (3) Electing the chairman and various committee members: It was resolved that Wang Jiean, with 13 votes, was elected chairman; Chen Yiting, with 10 votes, and Zhu Zhenhan, with 7 votes, were elected as general affairs committee members; and Ji Jiannan, with 7 votes, was elected as accounting committee member. (4) Reorganizing the design committee: It was resolved that in addition to the chairman and general affairs accounting committee members being ex officio members, Shen Shuyu, Sun Daosheng, Dong Hancheng, Wang Xingguang, Wang Zuocai, Fang Jiange, and Lu Xingzhuang would be designated as basic committee members, and each committee could nominate 24 celebrities and experts from all circles to be hired by the association to organize the design committee, to design the association's affairs and all strategies for the national goods industry. (5) Goods produced nationally should be marked with the national language: It was resolved to send another letter to various factories to implement this. (6) Petitioning the Zhejiang Provincial Government to redress the unjust case of Huachang: It was resolved to wait for the legal resolution. (7) Sending letters to various factories to purchase and manufacture military supplies machinery: It was resolved to send letters to the factories and solicit methods. (8) Relieving the plight of Wuzhou fish oil: It was resolved to send a letter to the Anti-Japanese Association, requesting the speedy return of the products to help merchants in need. (9) The Commercial News Agency's request for substantial assistance: It was resolved to send letters to various factories to provide substantial mutual assistance. (10) Requiring the National Goods Bank to effectively support national goods factories: It was resolved to send a letter to the bank, requesting it to effectively implement the original purpose of its organization. (11) Requesting the Nanchang Anti-Japanese Association to certify the products of Tianyuan: It was resolved to approve the letter of certification and send a letter to the Tianyuan factory to quickly correct the packaging. (12) The Qin County Anti-Japanese Association requested an investigation into the Huang salt case: It was resolved to send an inquiry to the manufacturer and trademark of Huang salt, in order to investigate and reply, and to certify that Tianyuan salt is indeed a national product. (13) Whether the association should participate in the work of the Shanghai Commercial Anti-Japanese Association: It was resolved to send a letter to the association, allowing the association to participate with five representatives to protect national goods. (14) Secret (15) Requesting another relief for Huachang's products and the slandering of procedures: It was resolved to publicly nominate Sun Daosheng and Wang Xingyao to jointly go with the representatives of the location to state the reasons for the case, in order to avoid punishment.

Yesterday, the Second Factory Representatives' Meeting of the National Goods Exhibition

The Third Factory Representatives' Meeting of the Third National Goods Exhibition in Zhabei was held yesterday afternoon at 6 PM in the auditorium of the Zhabei Chamber of Commerce. Sixty-four representatives, including those from the China Enamel Factory, attended. Chen Yiting was publicly elected as chairman. Zhang Baoshan, a member of the finance department, reported on the economic income and expenditure. The secretariat read out the letters from all circles requesting the association to extend the exhibition period. The following cases were then resolved: (1) The association should extend the exhibition period for three days due to the earnest requests of various groups and people from all walks of life in Zhabei. The opening ceremony will be held on the 31st of this month and will not be postponed again. (2) The publicity committee will continue to hold small-scale group parades. (3) The committee should raise appropriate compensation for the personnel protecting the exhibition site in various public affairs. (4) The charity fund has already been solicited from various factories, and the budget item of 200 yuan for the charity fund should be withdrawn and paid under the preparation item. (5) Collect exquisite samples from various factories to give to representatives from all circles as a souvenir. (6) Hold a scheduled narrative meal, a banquet for comrades who have supported the association's affairs, in order to reward their enthusiasm for protection.

Liu Shufan Resigns from Postal Savings and Remittances; Leaves Office Today

Liu Shufan, Director of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau, has served in the postal service for more than 30 years. After the establishment of the National Government, he was one of the people who recovered postal rights. He was then appointed as Director-General of Posts and concurrently as Director of Postal Affairs. He was also specially appointed as a plenipotentiary representative to attend the Universal Postal Congress and inspect postal services in various countries. After returning to China, he suggested to the National Government that a special agency must be established to manage savings and remittances, which was approved. He was appointed as Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau. The bureau has been in existence for two years, and it is said that its business has been very developed and its performance has been excellent. This time, his request to resign has been approved, and he has been hired as a consultant by the ministry. The vacancy will be filled by Yang Jianping. The handover is scheduled for the 28th.

The Telegraph Censorship Office Is Ordered to Close Down

Wu Guofang, a telegraph censor in this port, submitted a document to the Municipal Party Department yesterday stating: "According to the Songhu Garrison Command's Instruction No. 245, the Telegraph Censorship Office should be abolished and closed down immediately." Upon receiving this order, we complied with the order to close down on January 24 and notified the directors of the telegraph offices to stop censorship immediately. In accordance with the previous order, we hereby report the circumstances of the closure.

The Municipal Government Issues Instructions to Strictly Practice Economy

The Shanghai Municipal Government issued instructions yesterday to personnel in the government and affiliated bureaus, stating: "According to the Executive Yuan's instructions, in recent times, the country has suffered many misfortunes and frequent disasters, financial resources have become increasingly scarce, and the people's livelihoods have become increasingly strained. It is extremely difficult to maintain the economy. Unless the entire country, from top to bottom, strictly practices economy and eliminates extravagance, it will not be possible to cultivate vitality and avert danger. The motion to promote economy, which was passed by the Third Plenary Session of the Third Central Committee, has been followed by the Executive Yuan. Now that the national crisis has not yet subsided and the people's hardship has not been relieved, public and private expenditures must be tightened. All administrative agencies and their subordinate civil servants, who serve the country and take from the people, should share the burden, strictly practice economy, and strive to reduce all unnecessary expenditures. There should be no extravagance. All improper consumption and entertainment should be eliminated. By setting an example, we can eradicate the roots of corruption, change long-standing habits, and cultivate a culture of thrift. This is the key to saving the country. Apart from issuing separate orders, we hereby order you to comply and instruct all to comply.

The China General Edison Company Issues a Notice on Welfare Benefits for Employees

Regarding the employee benefits of the China General Edison Company, the company sets aside 10% of the employee's salary each year and names it the employee savings fund, which has been implemented since January 1924. As of the end of May of last year (1931), a total of more than 90,000 yuan has been saved. From June 1 of last year, the previous savings were stopped and new regulations were made. Therefore, although all employees have requested the company to return the savings to each individual, it is currently being negotiated. Suddenly, a misunderstanding occurred among the workers, who also requested the company to withdraw 60% of the employee savings and give it to the workers. After discussion by the board of directors, it was decided that the company has a worker welfare and education fund that is set aside annually. After signing the labor-capital treatment agreement in 1927, the worker welfare and education fund was transferred to the worker children's school expenses and then the savings were stopped. The current balance is also more than 9,000 yuan, with clear boundaries. Therefore, all the workers gathered at the company yesterday morning, asking the manager to accept the previous request. The Postal Workers' Union representative Zhu Xuefan and the director of the board, Du Yuesheng, sent representatives to the company to negotiate with both labor and capital. At 5 PM, everyone dispersed. The company's manager Lu Bohong issued two notices and posted them inside the company. (1) As a notice, according to the application of various employees, the company's total employee savings that have been set aside each year since January of the 13th year of the Republic of China (i.e., the Jiazi year) were terminated at the end of May of last year (1931). This savings fund should be requested from the company to be allocated and distributed immediately in order to conclude. It was submitted to the company's board of directors for a resolution. Although the above-mentioned welfare pension fund was set aside before the end of May of the 20th year, it should still be checked in accordance with the resolution of the meeting on February 23 of the 13th year. Employees can only receive it if they have served in the company for 12 years starting from March of the 13th year. Please ask the manager to notify all employees to check, etc. Therefore, it should be recorded and notified, so that everyone is aware. This is the notice. (2) Regarding the requests of all the workers in the company, the company expressed its acceptance, but it must be resolved at an emergency board of directors meeting next year. A reply will be given at noon the day after tomorrow. May all the workers work in peace and wait for a reply. This is the notice.

Local News

Anti-Japanese Association to Be Abolished 135

Municipal Government Orders Public Safety and Social Affairs Bureaus to Comply

The Municipal Government ordered the Public Safety Bureau yesterday to abolish all anti-Japanese associations in the city. The original order is excerpted below: "Order for compliance: Since our country suffered calamity, the people of this city, deeply concerned about their country, formed various anti-Japanese national salvation associations. Unfortunately, their actions were inappropriate, leading to numerous criticisms. Furthermore, local civic groups submitted petitions to the government, requesting relief. After careful consideration, the Mayor, in his unwavering loyalty to the nation, decided to resolutely stop them. Therefore, this order instructs the Bureau to immediately comply, and in conjunction with the Social Affairs Bureau, promptly abolish the said associations and report the handling status for verification. This is a crucial order."

Mayor Wu's Remarks: The current state of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee of all circles in this city seems to be close to a standstill. The industrial and commercial sectors have recently expressed their intention to withdraw. It is rumored that the Municipal Government also issued an order for its abolition yesterday. As this matter is of great importance, reporters specially interviewed Mayor Wu yesterday to inquire about the details. He replied as follows: "Since the September 18th Incident, with the country facing increasing difficulties, the public, driven by righteous indignation, rose up to engage in patriotic movements. Peaceful struggle is commendable, and the government would never forbid the people from being patriotic. However, in the current circumstances, the people should consider the nation's difficulties, ensuring that all actions remain within the bounds of law and order. This way, the government can continue to support the public while they advocate for their cause. Unfortunately, since its establishment, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee of all circles in this city has not followed legal procedures in its organization, and its actions have often exceeded the bounds of what is acceptable. Detaining goods and arresting people has repeatedly caused controversy. Their verdicts and punishments resemble those of a court. Moreover, the registration and confiscation of goods have been delayed for too long without resolution, causing deep distress to various chambers of commerce and trade associations, who have petitioned the government for relief. Various labor unions have also declared that such organizations only invite criticism and are insufficient for national salvation. The actions of the said Committee can be imagined. As the head of this city, during this critical period of national crisis, I must uphold the central government's authority and maintain overall stability as my sole responsibility. Shanghai is the financial hub of the country, and the lifeblood of industry and commerce. The Committee's actions, which have exceeded the bounds of what is acceptable, will inevitably affect order. To preserve local stability and social order, it is the government's duty to order its abolition. I have instructed the Public Safety and Social Affairs Bureaus to comply. In these difficult times, with the situation becoming increasingly severe, it is deeply regrettable that the actions of a patriotic organization have forced me to take such decisive measures. I only hope that the people of this country will become more vigilant and genuinely patriotic. Perseverance will eventually lead to success. Rushing into things impulsively will only lead to local chaos and national ruin. Patriotic actions taken in the wrong way will ultimately harm the country. I hope the media will urge the citizens to reflect deeply."

News of Various Organizations Withdrawing from the Abolished Anti-Japanese Association 136

Over One Hundred Trade Associations Submit Documents: The Shanghai Miscellaneous Grains and Oil Cake Trade Association, Yarn Trade Association, Seafood and Sundries Trade Association, Ginseng and Bird's Nest Trade Association, Medicinal Materials Trade Association, Hardware Trade Association, Coal Trade Association, Sausage Trade Association, Mercerized Cotton Weaving Trade Association, Cosmetics Trade Association, Cotton Cloth Trade Association, New Medicine Trade Association, Paper Trade Association, Southern Goods Trade Association, North-South Goods Exchange Trade Association, Rubber Hardware Vehicle Parts Trade Association, Sugar Trade Association, Department Store Trade Association, Seafood Shop Trade Association, Transportation Trade Association, Electrical Appliance Trade Association, Silk Fabric Trade Association, Flying Flower Trade Association, Coal and Stone Transportation Barge Trade Association, and over one hundred other trade associations submitted documents to the Municipal Government yesterday, requesting relief due to the mismanagement of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee of all circles in this city. (Omitted above) "Since the September 18th Incident, various sectors of this city, driven by righteous indignation, jointly organized the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee to engage in economic severance with Japan, which is indeed an important undertaking. However, the handling has not been entirely appropriate, leading to the resignation of various executive committee members in charge, weakening the organization day by day. Their actions have exceeded the bounds of what is acceptable, such as mistakenly detaining goods from various industries and arbitrarily suspending account books, which have been repeatedly negotiated but not yet returned. The amount of confiscated and registered Japanese goods is quite substantial, and there is still no way to dispose of them. With the year-end settlement period approaching rapidly, failure to provide prompt relief would seriously affect commercial stability. We have previously jointly petitioned the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to forward a letter to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Committee of all circles, setting a deadline for handling the matter. However, many days have passed without a response. In addition to informing the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to notify all business representatives to withdraw from the association, we respectfully submit this petition to your government for review. We hope that you will consider the importance of relieving the financial panic and strive to maintain stability. At the same time, we request that the Public Safety Bureau be ordered to effectively protect the confiscated goods in the various warehouses of the association in order to safeguard commerce." (Shanghai News Agency)

Middle School Anti-Japanese Association Petitions the Municipal Government: The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of Middle School Students in this city held an executive committee meeting at 1:00 PM yesterday. After the meeting, all executive committee members, including Wu Yuankan from Fudan Middle School, Xie Jinbiao from Shanghai Jiangwan Middle School, Yang Xikun from Shanghai Middle School, and Xiao Sizhi from Pudong Middle School, totaling fourteen people, went to the Municipal Government at 3:00 PM to petition. Their five demands were as follows: (1) Oppose the Municipal Government accepting the Japanese consulate's protest; (2) Release the workers arrested for anti-Japanese activities; (3) Guarantee the permanent public existence of anti-Japanese organizations; (4) Oppose the Municipal Council dissolving anti-Japanese organizations; (5) Oppose the Municipal Council closing down Chinese media outlets. As Mayor Wu and Secretary-General Yu were both away on official business, Guan Gong and Xiang Risi received them in turn. The group insisted on meeting with the Mayor or Secretary-General and persisted for a long time without success. They finally dispersed at 6:15 PM.

Meeting Report of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association (Datong News Agency):

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in this city held a continuous series of executive and standing committee meetings yesterday after the staff first held a meeting. The details are as follows: (1) Staff Meeting: The internal staff of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association convened a joint meeting yesterday morning. As a result of the discussion, Yang Haichang, Cai Liansheng (Inspection Department staff), Ju Zhengqiu, Hui Quan (Secretariat), Luo Deming, Jin Xiaodong, Wang Jinwu (Intelligence Department), Xie Hezong (Investigation Department), and Lü Zhongyuan (Propaganda Department) were appointed to go to the Postal Labor Union to find Standing Committee member Lu Jingshi and inquire about his intentions. At the same time, a notice was issued to all staff: "For notification: According to rumors, this association is facing closure. Whether this is true has not been confirmed. In order to maintain the situation and demonstrate the spirit of anti-Japanese resistance, all staff members are hereby notified to come to the association as usual and not to lightly believe rumors and cause unnecessary panic. Printed by the United Staff Association of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association." (2) Standing Committee Meeting: After the representatives dispatched by the staff met with Standing Committee member Lu Jingshi, Lu instructed all staff members to work with peace of mind and promised to take responsibility for convening a standing committee meeting. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, the meeting was convened on the fourth floor of the Ningbo Compatriots Association in Shanghai. The standing committee members present included Chu Huiseng, Yu Hualong, Fang Jiaobo (substituting for Chu Huiseng), Hu Fengxiang, Li Yongxiang, and Lu Jingshi. They first discussed the unresolved cases of confiscated Japanese goods and detained traitors. Therefore, the officials Liu Xiaochen, Bo Zipei, and Yang Xiangyun, who had been detained by the association for several days, were released, and the confiscated Japanese goods were unsealed, but only on the condition that the company publish an apology to the association in the newspaper. Next, they discussed the issue of the Anti-Japanese Association itself. Due to the gravity of the matter, it was postponed to the subsequent executive committee meeting for discussion and was therefore not discussed. (3) Executive Committee Discussion: At 5:00 PM last night, the executive committee meeting was convened. The executive committee members present included Wang Hanliang, Yu Hualong, Zhang Zilian, Zhang Yichen, Hu Fengxiang, Chu Huiseng, Zhu Xuefan, Wang Zhuping, Chen Peide, Wang Changyuan, and over thirty others. Chu Huiseng presided over the meeting, with Cao Zhigong and Tong Yikang as the recorders. They immediately discussed various external rumors and unreasonable demands from the Japanese side. After discussing until about 8:00 PM, they all agreed that the Anti-Japanese Association was initiated due to the Liaoning Incident and was a consistent demand of the people nationwide. As long as the Liaoning Incident is not resolved, the Anti-Japanese Association will continue to exist. Therefore, they should continue to work hard and carry out anti-Japanese national salvation work. As for the rumors that the Municipal Government has accepted demands from the Japanese side, they will wait for an official order from the Municipal Government. Changing the name of the Anti-Japanese Association is acceptable, but its goals and purpose are deeply engraved in the minds of the people and will not change. Secretary Cao Zhigong was then instructed to draft a circular instructing all staff members to carry on their work as usual. The meeting was then adjourned.

Meeting Report of the Shanghai County Anti-Japanese Association: The Shanghai County Anti-Japanese Association held its fifth plenary session of the Executive and Supervisory Committees yesterday morning in Beiqiao. Twenty committee members attended, chaired by Jiang Yanchou and recorded by Chen Guoan. After the formal procedures, the following items were discussed: (1) How the association should respond to the unreasonable demands made by the Japanese to the Municipal Government. The resolution was: (A) The Japanese forcibly demanding the cessation of anti-Japanese activities should be reported to the central government for severe rejection. (B) Volunteer troops should be organized as soon as possible for self-defense. (C) The county government should be requested to order the Public Security Bureau to step up precautions. (D) The Municipal Council should be questioned about the reasons for closing the Republic Daily newspaper. (E) All anti-Japanese associations in various regions should be notified by telegram to intensify their work. (2) Zhang Zuoxiang willingly colluded with foreigners and dared to publicly telegraph Jilin Acting Chairman Chen Yun, advising him to adopt a policy of non-resistance and surrender the territory. The association should issue a serious warning to him and ask Chairman Chen to fight to the end. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned.
